## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models population growth rate dP/dt as a function of time t and population P, which is the fundamental setup for population dynamics ODEs. The relationship likely involves density-dependent feedback mechanisms where growth rate depends on current population size.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Exponential (Malthusian) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited growth, density-independent)
- Logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (growth rate decreases logarithmically with population)
- Theta-logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized logistic with shape parameter)
- Allee effect (strong): dP_dt = c0 * P * (P * c1 - 1) * (1 - c2 * P) (growth fails below critical density)
- Allee effect (weak): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (c2 + P) (reduced growth at low density without extinction threshold)
- Beverton-Holt continuous: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (density-dependent with hyperbolic saturation)
- Quadratic density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 (simplest nonlinear density feedback)
- Cubic density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (Allee-type polynomial form)
- Richards growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (flexible sigmoidal growth model)
- Time-varying Malthusian: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * t) (exponential growth with time-dependent rate)
- Seasonal modulated logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) (logistic with periodic forcing)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (fractional-order density dependence)
- Von Bertalanffy population analog: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (anabolism-catabolism balance)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Density-dependent negative feedback → multiplicative factor (1 - c*P) or (1 - (c*P)**n) representing carrying capacity limitation
- Allee effect (positive density dependence at low P) → additional multiplicative factor (P - c) or (c + P) creating a minimum viable population
- Per-capita growth rate declining with P → dP_dt/P should be a decreasing function of P, suggesting forms like c0*(1 - c1*P) or c0*log(c1/P)
- Logarithmic density dependence → Gompertz-type log(c/P) factor indicates growth rate decays more slowly than linear at high density
- Periodic environmental forcing → multiplicative (1 + c*sin(c*t)) or (1 + c*cos(c*t)) modulating an autonomous growth term
- Population extinction boundary → dP_dt must equal zero when P=0, enforcing at least one multiplicative P factor
- Multiple equilibria in population → polynomial in P with degree ≥ 3 (e.g., cubic) allowing for multiple roots/steady states
- Saturating resource competition → rational form P/(1 + c*P) replacing linear P term, analogous to Michaelis-Menten kinetics in resource uptake

c8) + c9/(c7*t + c8)"]

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the Ground Truth:

**GT: 0.954*(1 - P/96.907)*P + 0.954*P^(1/3)**

Expanding: **GT = 0.954*P - (0.954/96.907)*P² + 0.954*P^(1/3)**

This simplifies to: **GT = c_a*P² + c_b*P + c_c*P^(1/3)** where c_a = -0.00984..., c_b = 0.954, c_c = 0.954.

So the GT has three basis functions: **P², P, and P^(1/3)**, with no dependence on t.

Let me check each candidate systematically.

For candidates with time-dependent terms, those terms must be eliminable (coefficients set to 0). For candidates with extra terms like exp, log, sin, they must also be eliminable.

**Key structural requirement:** The candidate must be reducible to `a*P² + b*P + c*P^(1/3)` (possibly with a constant term that can be zeroed).

Let me go through each:

**Candidate 1:** P²c0 + Pc1 + Pc2*(Pc3)^c4 + c5*sin(c6*t+c7)
Set c5=0 to kill sin term. Remaining: P²c0 + Pc1 + Pc2*(Pc3)^c4 = P²c0 + Pc1 + c2*c3^c4 * P^(1+c4). Set c4 = -2/3, then P^(1+c4) = P^(1/3). ✓
Candidate 1 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 2:** P³c0 + P²c1 + P²c2 + Pc3 + Pc4 + P^c5*c6 + c7*exp(P^c8*c9)
Set c0=0, c7=0 (or c9=0 makes exp=exp(0)... no, need c7=0). Then: P²(c1+c2) + P(c3+c4) + c6*P^c5. Set c5=1/3. ✓
